          <a data-permalink-href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blame/5a6c7f678a8f56cc169b3f473c99ce071a67e603/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/data-science/data-science-in-the-wild.md" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blame/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/data-science/data-science-in-the-wild.md" group_item="true" data-hotkey="b" data-view-component="true" class="js-update-url-with-hash js-permalink-replaceable-link Button--secondary Button--small Button">    <span class="Button-content">
      <span class="Button-label">Blame</span>
    </span>
</a>  
    </div>

<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science-in-the-real-world" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science-in-the-real-world"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science in the real world</h1>
<p dir="auto">We're almost at the end of this learning journey!</p>
<p dir="auto">We started with definitions of data science and ethics, explored various tools &amp; techniques for data analysis and visualization, reviewed the data science lifecycle, and looked at scaling and automating data science workflows with cloud computing services. So, you're probably wondering: <em>"How exactly do I map all these learnings to real-world contexts?"</em></p>
<p dir="auto">In this section, we'll explore real-world applications of data science across industries and dive into specific examples in the research, digital humanities, and sustainability, contexts. We'll look at student project opportunities and conclude with useful resources to help you continue your learning journey!</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science--industry" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science--industry"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science + industry</h2>
<p dir="auto">Thanks to the democratization of AI, developers are now finding it easier to design and integrate AI-driven decision-making and data-driven insights into user experiences and development workflows. Here are a few examples of how data science is "applied" to real-world applications across the industry:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://www.wired.com/2015/10/can-learn-epic-failure-google-flu-trends/" rel="nofollow">Google Flu Trends</a> used data science to correlate search terms with flu trends. While the approach had flaws, it raised awareness of the possibilities (and challenges) of data-driven healthcare predictions.</li>
<li><a href="https://www.technologyreview.com/2018/11/21/139000/how-ups-uses-ai-to-outsmart-bad-weather/" rel="nofollow">UPS Routing Predictions</a> - explains how UPS uses data science and machine learning to predict optimal routes for delivery, taking into account weather conditions, traffic patterns, delivery deadlines, and more.</li>
<li><a href="http://chriswhong.github.io/nyctaxi/" rel="nofollow">NYC Taxicab Route Visualization</a> - data gathered using <a href="https://chriswhong.com/open-data/foil_nyc_taxi/" rel="nofollow">Freedom Of Information Laws</a> helped visualize a day in the life of NYC cabs, helping us understand how they navigate the busy city, the money they make, and the duration of trips over each 24 hours.</li>
<li><a href="https://eng.uber.com/dsw/" rel="nofollow">Uber Data Science Workbench</a> - uses data (on pickup &amp; dropoff locations, trip duration, preferred routes, etc.) gathered from millions of uber trips <em>daily</em> to build a data analytics tool to help with pricing, safety, fraud detection, and navigation decisions.</li>
<li><a href="https://towardsdatascience.com/scope-of-analytics-in-sports-world-37ed09c39860" rel="nofollow">Sports Analytics</a> - focuses on <em>predictive analytics</em> (team and player analysis - think <a href="https://datasciencedegree.wisconsin.edu/blog/moneyball-proves-importance-big-data-big-ideas/" rel="nofollow">Moneyball</a> - and fan management) and <em>data visualization</em> (team &amp; fan dashboards, games, etc.) with applications like talent scouting, sports gambling, and inventory/venue management.</li>
<li><a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-in-banking/" rel="nofollow">Data Science in Banking</a> - highlights the value of data science in the finance industry with applications ranging from risk modeling and fraud detection, to customer segmentation, real-time prediction, and recommender systems. Predictive analytics also drive critical measures like <a href="https://dzone.com/articles/using-big-data-and-predictive-analytics-for-credit" rel="nofollow">credit scores</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-in-healthcare/" rel="nofollow">Data Science in Healthcare</a> - highlights applications like medical imaging (e.g., MRI, X-Ray, CT-Scan), genomics (DNA sequencing), drug development (risk assessment, success prediction), predictive analytics (patient care &amp; supply logistics), disease tracking &amp; prevention, etc.</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="---
name: 'Data Science applications in the real world'
---
Data Science applications in the real world{cite}`6_amazing_data_science_applications`"><pre lang="{figure}" class="notranslate"><code>---
name: 'Data Science applications in the real world'
---
Data Science applications in the real world{cite}`6_amazing_data_science_applications`
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The figure shows other domains and examples for applying data science techniques. Want to explore other applications? Check out the <a href="#self-study">Self study</a> section below.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science--research" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science--research"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science + research</h2>
<p dir="auto">While real-world applications often focus on industry use cases at scale, <em>research</em> applications and projects can be useful from two perspectives:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><em>innovation opportunities</em> - explore rapid prototyping of advanced concepts and testing of user experiences for next-generation applications.</li>
<li><em>deployment challenges</em> - investigate potential harms or unintended consequences of Data Science technologies in real-world contexts.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">For students, these research projects can provide both learning and collaboration opportunities that can improve your understanding of the topic, and broaden your awareness and engagement with relevant people or teams working in areas of interest. So what do research projects look like and how can they make an impact?</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's look at one example - the <a href="http://gendershades.org/overview.html" rel="nofollow">MIT Gender Shades Study</a> from Joy Buolamwini (MIT Media Labs) with a <a href="http://proceedings.mlr.press/v81/buolamwini18a/buolamwini18a.pdf" rel="nofollow">signature research paper</a> co-authored with Timnit Gebru (then at Microsoft Research) that focused on,</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>What:</strong> The objective of the research project was to <em>evaluate bias present in automated facial analysis algorithms and datasets</em> based on gender and skin type.</li>
<li><strong>Why:</strong> Facial analysis is used in areas like law enforcement, airport security, hiring systems and more - contexts where inaccurate classifications (e.g., due to bias) can cause potential economic and social harm to affected individuals or groups. Understanding (and eliminating or mitigating) biases is key to fairness in usage.</li>
<li><strong>How:</strong> Researchers recognized that existing benchmarks used predominantly lighter-skinned subjects, and curated a new data set (1000+ images) that was <em>more balanced</em> by gender and skin type. The data set was used to evaluate the accuracy of three gender classification products (from Microsoft, IBM &amp; Face++).</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Results showed that though overall classification accuracy was good, there was a noticeable difference in error rates between various subgroups - with <strong>misgendering</strong> being higher for females or persons with darker skin types, indicative of bias.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Key Outcomes:</strong> Raised awareness that data science needs more <em>representative datasets</em> (balanced subgroups) and more <em>inclusive teams</em> (diverse backgrounds) to recognize and eliminate or mitigate such biases earlier in AI solutions. Research efforts like this are also instrumental in many organizations defining principles and practices for <em>responsible AI</em> to improve fairness across their AI products and processes.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Want to learn about relevant research efforts in Microsoft?</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Check out <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/research/research-area/artificial-intelligence/?facet%5Btax%5D%5Bmsr-research-area%5D%5B%5D=13556&amp;facet%5Btax%5D%5Bmsr-content-type%5D%5B%5D=msr-project" rel="nofollow">Microsoft Research Projects</a> on Artificial Intelligence.</li>
<li>Explore student projects from <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/academic-program/data-science-summer-school/" rel="nofollow">Microsoft Research Data Science Summer School</a>.</li>
<li>Check out the <a href="https://fairlearn.org/" rel="nofollow">Fairlearn</a> project and <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/ai/responsible-ai?activetab=pivot1%3aprimaryr6" rel="nofollow">Responsible AI</a> initiatives.</li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science--humanities" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science--humanities"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science + humanities</h2>
<p dir="auto">Digital Humanities <a href="https://digitalhumanities.stanford.edu/about-dh-stanford" rel="nofollow">has been defined</a> as "a collection of practices and approaches combining computational methods with the humanistic inquiry". <a href="https://digitalhumanities.stanford.edu/projects" rel="nofollow">Stanford projects</a> like <em>"rebooting history"</em> and <em>"poetic thinking"</em> illustrate the linkage between <a href="https://digitalhumanities.stanford.edu/digital-humanities-and-data-science" rel="nofollow">Digital Humanities and Data Science</a> - emphasizing techniques like network analysis, information visualization, and spatial and text analysis that can help us revisit historical and literary data sets to derive new insights and perspectives.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Want to explore and extend a project in this space?</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">Check out <a href="https://gist.github.com/jlooper/ce4d102efd057137bc000db796bfd671">"Emily Dickinson and the Meter of Mood"</a> - a great example from <a href="https://twitter.com/jenlooper" rel="nofollow">Jen Looper</a> that asks how we can use data science to revisit familiar poetry and re-evaluate its meaning and the contributions of its author in new contexts. For instance, <em>can we predict the season in which a poem was authored by analyzing its tone or sentiment</em> - and what does this tell us about the author's state of mind over the relevant period?</p>
<p dir="auto">To answer that question, we follow the steps of our data science lifecycle:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://gist.github.com/jlooper/ce4d102efd057137bc000db796bfd671#acquiring-the-dataset"><strong>Data Acquisition</strong></a> - to collect a relevant dataset for analysis. Options include using an API (e.g., <a href="https://poetrydb.org/index.html" rel="nofollow">Poetry DB API</a>) or scraping web pages (e.g., <a href="https://www.gutenberg.org/files/12242/12242-h/12242-h.htm" rel="nofollow">Project Gutenberg</a>) using tools like <a href="https://scrapy.org/" rel="nofollow">Scrapy</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://gist.github.com/jlooper/ce4d102efd057137bc000db796bfd671#clean-the-data"><strong>Data Cleaning</strong></a> - explains how text can be formatted, sanitized and simplified using basic tools like Visual Studio Code and Microsoft Excel.</li>
<li><a href="https://gist.github.com/jlooper/ce4d102efd057137bc000db796bfd671#working-with-the-data-in-a-notebook"><strong>Data Analysis</strong></a> - explains how we can now import the dataset into "Notebooks" for analysis using Python packages (like pandas, NumPy and matplotlib) to organize and visualize the data.</li>
<li><a href="https://gist.github.com/jlooper/ce4d102efd057137bc000db796bfd671#sentiment-analysis-using-cognitive-services"><strong>Sentiment Analysis</strong></a> - explains how we can integrate cloud services like Text Analytics, using low-code tools like <a href="https://flow.microsoft.com/en-us/" rel="nofollow">Power Automate</a> for automated data processing workflows.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Using this workflow, we can explore the seasonal impacts on the sentiment of the poems, and help us fashion our own perspectives on the author. Try it out yourself - then extend the notebook to ask other questions or visualize the data in new ways!</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="You can use some of the tools in the [Digital Humanities toolkit](https://github.com/Digital-Humanities-Toolkit) to pursue these avenues of inquiry"><pre lang="{note}" class="notranslate"><code>You can use some of the tools in the [Digital Humanities toolkit](https://github.com/Digital-Humanities-Toolkit) to pursue these avenues of inquiry
</code></pre></div>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science--sustainability" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science--sustainability"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science + sustainability</h2>
<p dir="auto">The <a href="https://sdgs.un.org/2030agenda" rel="nofollow">2030 Agenda For Sustainable Development</a> - adopted by all United Nations members in 2015 - identifies 17 goals including ones that focus on <strong>Protecting the Planet</strong> from degradation and the impact of climate change. The <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/sustainability" rel="nofollow">Microsoft Sustainability</a> initiative supports these goals by exploring ways in which technology solutions can support and build more sustainable futures with a <a href="https://dev.to/azure/a-visual-guide-to-sustainable-software-engineering-53hh" rel="nofollow">focus on 4 goals</a> - being carbon negative, water positive, zero waste, and bio-diverse by 2030.</p>
<p dir="auto">Tackling these challenges in a scalable and timely manner requires cloud-scale thinking - and large-scale data. The <a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/" rel="nofollow">Planetary Computer</a> initiative provides 4 components to help data scientists and developers in this effort:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/catalog" rel="nofollow">Data Catalog</a> - with petabytes of Earth Systems data (free &amp; Azure-hosted).</li>
<li><a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/docs/reference/stac/" rel="nofollow">Planetary API</a> - to help users search for relevant data across space and time.</li>
<li><a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/docs/overview/environment/" rel="nofollow">Hub</a> - managed environment for scientists to process massive geospatial datasets.</li>
<li><a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/applications" rel="nofollow">Applications</a> - showcase use cases &amp; tools for sustainability insights.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>The Planetary Computer Project is currently in preview (as of Sep 2021)</strong> - here's how you can get started contributing to sustainability solutions using data science.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/account/request" rel="nofollow">Request access</a> to start exploration and connect with peers.</li>
<li><a href="https://planetarycomputer.microsoft.com/docs/overview/about" rel="nofollow">Explore documentation</a> to understand supported datasets and APIs.</li>
<li>Explore applications like <a href="https://analytics-lab.org/ecosystemmonitoring/" rel="nofollow">Ecosystem Monitoring</a> for inspiration on application ideas.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Think about how you can use data visualization to expose or amplify relevant insights into areas like climate change and deforestation. Or think about how insights can be used to create new user experiences that motivate behavioral changes for more sustainable living.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science--students" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science--students"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science + students</h2>
<p dir="auto">We've talked about real-world applications in industry and research, and explored data science application examples in digital humanities and sustainability. So how can you build your skills and share your expertise as a data science beginner?</p>
<p dir="auto">Here are some examples of data science student projects to inspire you.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/academic-program/data-science-summer-school/#!projects" rel="nofollow">MSR Data Science Summer School</a> with GitHub <a href="https://github.com/msr-ds3">projects</a> exploring topics like:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/video/data-science-summer-school-2019-replicating-an-empirical-analysis-of-racial-differences-in-police-use-of-force/" rel="nofollow">Racial Bias in Police Use of Force</a> | <a href="https://github.com/msr-ds3/stop-question-frisk">Github</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/video/data-science-summer-school-2018-exploring-the-reliability-of-the-nyc-subway-system/" rel="nofollow">Reliability of NYC Subway System</a> | <a href="https://github.com/msr-ds3/nyctransit">Github</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="https://claremont.maps.arcgis.com/apps/Cascade/index.html?appid=bdf2aef0f45a4674ba41cd373fa23afc" rel="nofollow">Digitizing Material Culture: Exploring socio-economic distributions in Sirkap</a>- from <a href="https://twitter.com/ornelladotcom" rel="nofollow">Ornella Altunyan</a> and team at Claremont, using <a href="https://storymaps.arcgis.com/" rel="nofollow">ArcGIS StoryMaps</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-self-study" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#self-study"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Self study</h2>
<p dir="auto">Want to explore more use cases? Here are a few relevant articles:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://builtin.com/data-science/data-science-applications-examples" rel="nofollow">17 Data Science Applications and Examples</a> - Jul 2021</li>
<li><a href="https://myblindbird.com/data-science-applications-real-world/" rel="nofollow">11 Breathtaking Data Science Applications in Real World</a> - May 2021</li>
<li><a href="https://towardsdatascience.com/data-science-in-the-real-world/home" rel="nofollow">Data Science In The Real World</a> - Article Collection</li>
<li>Data Science In: <a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-in-education/" rel="nofollow">Education</a>, <a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-in-agriculture/" rel="nofollow">Agriculture</a>, <a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-in-finance/" rel="nofollow">Finance</a>, <a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-at-movies/" rel="nofollow">Movies</a> &amp; more.</li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-your-turn-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#your-turn-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Your turn! <g-emoji class="g-emoji" alias="rocket" fallback-src="https://github.githubassets.com/images/icons/emoji/unicode/1f680.png"></g-emoji></h2>
<p dir="auto">Search for articles that recommend data science projects that are beginner friendly - like <a href="https://www.upgrad.com/blog/data-science-project-ideas-topics-beginners/" rel="nofollow">these 50 topic areas</a> or <a href="https://www.intellspot.com/data-science-project-ideas" rel="nofollow">these 21 project ideas</a> or <a href="https://data-flair.training/blogs/data-science-project-ideas/" rel="nofollow">these 16 projects with source code</a> that you can deconstruct and remix. And don't forget to blog about your learning journeys and share your insights with all of us.</p>
<p dir="auto">Assignment - <a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/assignments/data-science/explore-a-planetary-computer-dataset.md">Explore A Planetary Computer Dataset</a></p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-acknowledgments" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#acknowledgments"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Acknowledgments</h2>

<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science-in-the-cloud" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science-in-the-cloud"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science in the cloud</h1>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/cloud-picture.jpeg"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/cloud-picture.jpeg" alt="cloud-picture" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Photo by <a href="https://unsplash.com/@ilumire" rel="nofollow">Jelleke Vanooteghem</a> from <a href="https://unsplash.com/s/photos/cloud?orientation=landscape" rel="nofollow">Unsplash</a></p>
</blockquote>
<p dir="auto">When it comes to doing data science with big data, the cloud can be a game changer. In the next three sections, we are going to see what the cloud is and why it can be very helpful. We are also going to explore a heart failure dataset and build a model to help assess the probability of someone having heart failure. We will use the power of the cloud to train, deploy and consume a model in two different ways. One way uses only the user interface in a Low code/No code fashion, and the other way uses the Azure Machine Learning Software Developer Kit (Azure ML SDK).</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/project-schema.png"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/project-schema.png" alt="project-schema" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<hr>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=""><pre lang="{tableofcontents}" class="notranslate"><code></code></pre></div>
</article>
  </div>

    <div class="d-flex hide-lg hide-xl flex-order-2 flex-grow-0">

<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-introduction" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#introduction"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Introduction</h1>
<p dir="auto">In this section, you will learn the fundamental principles of the cloud, then you will see why it can be interesting for you to use cloud services to run your data science projects and we'll look at some examples of data science projects run in the cloud.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-what-is-the-cloud" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#what-is-the-cloud"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>What is the cloud?</h2>
<p dir="auto">The Cloud, or Cloud Computing, is the delivery of a wide range of pay-as-you-go computing services hosted on infrastructure over the internet. Services include solutions such as storage, databases, networking, software, analytics, and intelligent services.</p>
<p dir="auto">We usually differentiate the Public, Private and Hybrid clouds as follows:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Public cloud: a public cloud is owned and operated by a third-party cloud service provider which delivers its computing resources over the Internet to the public.</li>
<li>Private cloud: refers to cloud computing resources used exclusively by a single business or organization, with services and infrastructure maintained on a private network.</li>
<li>Hybrid cloud: the hybrid cloud is a system that combines public and private clouds. Users opt for an on-premises data center while allowing data and applications to be run on one or more public clouds.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Most cloud computing services fall into three categories: Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS), Platform as a Service (PaaS) and Software as a Service (SaaS).</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS): users rent an IT infrastructure such as servers and virtual machines (VMs), storage, networks, operating systems</li>
<li>Platform as a Service (PaaS): users rent an environment for developing, testing, delivering, and managing software applications. Users dont need to worry about setting up or managing the underlying infrastructure of servers, storage, network, and databases needed for development.</li>
<li>Software as a Service (SaaS): users get access to software applications over the Internet, on-demand and typically on a subscription basis. Users dont need to worry about hosting and managing the software application, the underlying infrastructure or the maintenance, like software upgrades and security patching.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Some of the largest Cloud providers are Amazon Web Services, Google Cloud Platform and Microsoft Azure.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-why-choose-the-cloud-for-data-science" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#why-choose-the-cloud-for-data-science"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Why choose the cloud for Data Science?</h2>
<p dir="auto">Developers and IT professionals chose to work with the Cloud for many reasons, including the following:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Innovation: you can power your applications by integrating innovative services created by Cloud providers directly into your apps.</li>
<li>Flexibility: you only pay for the services that you need and can choose from a wide range of services. You typically pay as you go and adapt your services according to your evolving needs.</li>
<li>Budget: you dont need to make initial investments to purchase hardware and software, set up and run on-site data centers and you can just pay for what you use.</li>
<li>Scalability: your resources can scale according to the needs of your project, which means that your apps can use more or less computing power, storage and bandwidth, by adapting to external factors at any given time.</li>
<li>Productivity: you can focus on your business rather than spending time on tasks that can be managed by someone else, such as managing data centers.</li>
<li>Reliability: Cloud Computing offers several ways to continuously back up your data and you can set up disaster recovery plans to keep your business and services going, even in times of crisis.</li>
<li>Security: you can benefit from policies, technologies and controls that strengthen the security of your project.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">These are some of the most common reasons why people choose to use Cloud services. Now that we have a better understanding of what the Cloud is and what its main benefits are, let's look more specifically into the jobs of Data scientists and developers working with data, and how the Cloud can help them with several challenges they might face:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Storing large amounts of data: instead of buying, managing and protecting big servers, you can store your data directly in the cloud, with solutions such as Azure Cosmos DB, Azure SQL Database and Azure Data Lake Storage.</li>
<li>Performing Data Integration: data integration is an essential part of Data Science, that lets you make a transition from data collection to taking action. With data integration services offered in the cloud, you can collect, transform and integrate data from various sources into a single data warehouse, with Data Factory.</li>
<li>Processing data: processing vast amounts of data requires a lot of computing power, and not everyone has access to machines powerful enough for that, which is why many people choose to directly harness the clouds huge computing power to run and deploy their solutions.</li>
<li>Using data analytics services: cloud services like Azure Synapse Analytics, Azure Stream Analytics and Azure Databricks to help you turn your data into actionable insights.</li>
<li>Using Machine Learning and data intelligence services: Instead of starting from scratch, you can use machine learning algorithms offered by the cloud provider, with services such as AzureML. You can also use cognitive services such as speech-to-text, text-to-speech, computer vision and more.</li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-examples-of-data-science-in-the-cloud" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#examples-of-data-science-in-the-cloud"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Examples of Data Science in the cloud</h2>
<p dir="auto">Lets make this more tangible by looking at a couple of scenarios.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-real-time-social-media-sentiment-analysis" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#real-time-social-media-sentiment-analysis"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Real-time social media sentiment analysis</h3>
<p dir="auto">Well start with a scenario commonly studied by people who start with machine learning: social media sentiment analysis in real time.</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's say you run a news media website and you want to leverage live data to understand what content your readers could be interested in. To know more about that, you can build a program that performs real-time sentiment analysis of data from Twitter publications, on topics that are relevant to your readers.</p>
<p dir="auto">The key indicators you will look at are the volume of tweets on specific topics (hashtags) and sentiment, which is established using analytics tools that perform sentiment analysis around the specified topics.</p>
<p dir="auto">The steps necessary to create this project are as follows:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Create an event hub for streaming input, which will collect data from Twitter.</li>
<li>Configure and start a Twitter client application, which will call the Twitter Streaming APIs.</li>
<li>Create a Stream Analytics job.</li>
<li>Specify the job input and query.</li>
<li>Create an output sink and specify the job output.</li>
<li>Start the job.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">To view the full process, check out the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/stream-analytics/stream-analytics-twitter-sentiment-analysis-trends?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID30411099" rel="nofollow">documentation</a>.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-scientific-papers-analysis" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#scientific-papers-analysis"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Scientific papers analysis</h3>
<p dir="auto">Lets take another example of a project created by <a href="http://soshnikov.com" rel="nofollow">Dmitry Soshnikov</a>, one of the authors of this curriculum.</p>
<p dir="auto">Dmitry created a tool that analyses COVID papers. By reviewing this project, you will see how you can create a tool that extracts knowledge from scientific papers, gains insights and helps researchers navigate through large collections of papers in an efficient way.</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's see the different steps used for this:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Extracting and pre-processing information with <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/cognitive-services/text-analytics/how-tos/text-analytics-for-health?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Text Analytics for Health</a>.</li>
<li>Using <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/services/machine-learning?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Azure ML</a> to parallelize the processing.</li>
<li>Storing and querying information with <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/services/cosmos-db?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Cosmos DB</a>.</li>
<li>Create an interactive dashboard for data exploration and visualization using Power BI.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">To see the full process, visit <a href="https://soshnikov.com/science/analyzing-medical-papers-with-azure-and-text-analytics-for-health/" rel="nofollow">Dmitrys blog</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">As you can see, we can leverage Cloud services in many ways to perform Data Science.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-self-study" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#self-study"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Self study</h2>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/overview/what-is-cloud-computing?ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">What Is Cloud Computing? A Beginners Guide | Microsoft Azure</a></li>
<li><a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/stream-analytics/stream-analytics-twitter-sentiment-analysis-trends?ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Social media analysis with Azure Stream Analytics | Microsoft Learn</a></li>
<li><a href="https://soshnikov.com/science/analyzing-medical-papers-with-azure-and-text-analytics-for-health/" rel="nofollow">Analyzing COVID Medical Papers with Azure and Text Analytics for Health</a></li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-your-turn-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#your-turn-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Your turn! <g-emoji class="g-emoji" alias="rocket" fallback-src="https://github.githubassets.com/images/icons/emoji/unicode/1f680.png"></g-emoji></h2>
<p dir="auto"><a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/assignments/data-science/market-research.md">Market research</a></p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-acknowledgments" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#acknowledgments"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Acknowledgments</h2>
