<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-data-science-in-the-cloud-the-azure-ml-sdk-way" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#data-science-in-the-cloud-the-azure-ml-sdk-way"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Data Science in the cloud: The "Azure ML SDK" way</h1>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-introduction" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#introduction"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Introduction</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-what-is-azure-ml-sdk" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#what-is-azure-ml-sdk"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>What is Azure ML SDK?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Data scientists and AI developers use the Azure Machine Learning SDK to build and run Machine Learning workflows with the Azure Machine Learning service. You can interact with the service in any Python environment, including Jupyter Notebooks, Visual Studio Code, or your favorite Python IDE.</p>
<p dir="auto">Key areas of the SDK include:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Explore, prepare and manage the lifecycle of your datasets used in Machine Learning experiments.</li>
<li>Manage cloud resources for monitoring, logging, and organizing your Machine Learning experiments.</li>
<li>Train models either locally or by using cloud resources, including GPU-accelerated model training.</li>
<li>Use automated Machine Learning, which accepts configuration parameters and training data. It automatically iterates through algorithms and hyperparameter settings to find the best model for running predictions.</li>
<li>Deploy web services to convert your trained models into RESTful services that can be consumed in any application.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/overview/azure/ml?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Learn more about the Azure Machine Learning SDK</a></p>
<p dir="auto">In the <a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/data-science/data-science-in-the-cloud/the-low-code-no-code-way.md">previous section</a>, we saw how to train, deploy and consume a model in a Low code/No code fashion. We used the Heart Failure dataset to generate and Heart failure prediction model. In this section, we are going to do the exact same thing but using the Azure Machine Learning SDK.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/project-schema.PNG"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/project-schema.PNG" alt="project-schema" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-heart-failure-prediction-project-and-dataset-introduction" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#heart-failure-prediction-project-and-dataset-introduction"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Heart failure prediction project and dataset introduction</h3>
<p dir="auto">Check <a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/data-science/data-science-in-the-cloud/the-low-code-no-code-way.md">here</a> the Heart failure prediction project and dataset introduction.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-training-a-model-with-the-azure-ml-sdk" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#training-a-model-with-the-azure-ml-sdk"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Training a model with the Azure ML SDK</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-create-an-azure-ml-workspace" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#create-an-azure-ml-workspace"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Create an Azure ML workspace</h3>
<p dir="auto">For simplicity, we are going to work on a Jupyter Notebook. This implies that you already have a Workspace and a compute instance. If you already have a Workspace, you can directly jump to section 2.3 Notebook creation.</p>
<p dir="auto">If not, please follow the instructions in section <strong>2.1 Create an Azure ML workspace</strong> in the <a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/data-science/data-science-in-the-cloud/the-low-code-no-code-way.md">previous section</a> to create a workspace.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-create-a-compute-instance" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#create-a-compute-instance"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Create a compute instance</h3>
<p dir="auto">In the <a href="https://ml.azure.com/" rel="nofollow">Azure ML workspace</a> that we created earlier, go to the compute menu and you will see the different compute resources available</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/compute-instance-1.PNG"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/compute-instance-1.PNG" alt="compute-instance-1" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Let's create a compute instance to provision a Jupyter Notebook.</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Click on the + New button.</li>
<li>Give a name to your compute instance.</li>
<li>Choose your options: CPU or GPU, VM size and core number.</li>
<li>Click in the Create button.</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">Congratulations, you have just created a compute instance! We will use this compute instance to create a Notebook in the <a href="#23-creating-notebooks">Creating Notebooks section</a>.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-loading-the-dataset" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#loading-the-dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Loading the dataset</h3>
<p dir="auto">Refer to the <a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/data-science/data-science-in-the-cloud/the-low-code-no-code-way.md">previous section</a> in the section <a href="#loading-the-dataset">Loading the dataset</a> if you have not uploaded the dataset yet.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-creating-notebooks" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#creating-notebooks"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Creating Notebooks</h3>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="For the next step you can either create a new notebook from scratch, or you can upload the [notebook we created](../../assignments/data-science/data-science-in-the-cloud-the-azure-ml-sdk-way.ipynb) in you Azure ML Studio. To upload it, simply click on the &quot;Notebook&quot; menu and upload the notebook."><pre lang="{note}" class="notranslate"><code>For the next step you can either create a new notebook from scratch, or you can upload the [notebook we created](../../assignments/data-science/data-science-in-the-cloud-the-azure-ml-sdk-way.ipynb) in you Azure ML Studio. To upload it, simply click on the "Notebook" menu and upload the notebook.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Notebooks are a really important part of the data science process. They can be used to Conduct Exploratory Data Analysis (EDA), call out to a computer cluster to train a model, and call out to an inference cluster to deploy an endpoint.</p>
<p dir="auto">To create a Notebook, we need a compute node that is serving out the Jupyter Notebook instance. Go back to the <a href="https://ml.azure.com/" rel="nofollow">Azure ML workspace</a> and click on Compute instances. In the list of compute instances, you should see the <a href="#create-a-compute-instance">compute instance we created earlier</a>.</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>In the Applications section, click on the Jupyter option.</li>
<li>Tick the "Yes, I understand" box and click on the Continue button.
<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/notebook-1.PNG"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/notebook-1.PNG" alt="notebook-1" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></li>
<li>This should open a new browser tab with your Jupyter Notebook instance as follow. Click on the "New" button to create a notebook.</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/notebook-2.PNG"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/notebook-2.PNG" alt="notebook-2" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Now that we have a Notebook, we can start training the model with Azure ML SDK.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-training-a-model" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#training-a-model"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Training a model</h3>
<p dir="auto">First of all, if you ever have a doubt, refer to the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/overview/azure/ml?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Azure ML SDK documentation</a>. It contains all the necessary information to understand the modules we are going to see in this section.</p>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-setup-workspace-experiment-compute-cluster-and-dataset" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#setup-workspace-experiment-compute-cluster-and-dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Setup Workspace, experiment, compute cluster and dataset</h4>
<p dir="auto">You need to load the <code>workspace</code> from the configuration file using the following code:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from azureml.core import Workspace
ws = Workspace.from_config()"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">core</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">Workspace</span>
<span class="pl-s1">ws</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Workspace</span>.<span class="pl-en">from_config</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This returns an object of type <code>Workspace</code> that represents the workspace. You need to create an <code>experiment</code> using the following code:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from azureml.core import Experiment
experiment_name = 'aml-experiment'
experiment = Experiment(ws, experiment_name)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">core</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">Experiment</span>
<span class="pl-s1">experiment_name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'aml-experiment'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">experiment</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Experiment</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ws</span>, <span class="pl-s1">experiment_name</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">To get or create an experiment from a workspace, you request the experiment using the experiment name. Experiment name must be 3-36 characters, start with a letter or a number, and can only contain letters, numbers, underscores, and dashes. If the experiment is not found in the workspace, a new experiment is created.</p>
<p dir="auto">Now you need to create a compute cluster for the training using the following code. Note that this step can take a few minutes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from azureml.core.compute import AmlCompute

aml_name = &quot;heart-f-cluster&quot;
try:
    aml_compute = AmlCompute(ws, aml_name)
    print('Found existing AML compute context.')
except:
    print('Creating new AML compute context.')
    aml_config = AmlCompute.provisioning_configuration(vm_size=&quot;Standard_D2_v2&quot;, min_nodes=1, max_nodes=3)
    aml_compute = AmlCompute.create(ws, name=aml_name, provisioning_configuration=aml_config)
    aml_compute.wait_for_completion(show_output=True)

cts = ws.compute_targets
compute_target = cts[aml_name]"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">core</span>.<span class="pl-s1">compute</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">AmlCompute</span>

<span class="pl-s1">aml_name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"heart-f-cluster"</span>
<span class="pl-k">try</span>:
    <span class="pl-s1">aml_compute</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">AmlCompute</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ws</span>, <span class="pl-s1">aml_name</span>)
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Found existing AML compute context.'</span>)
<span class="pl-k">except</span>:
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Creating new AML compute context.'</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">aml_config</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">AmlCompute</span>.<span class="pl-en">provisioning_configuration</span>(<span class="pl-s1">vm_size</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">"Standard_D2_v2"</span>, <span class="pl-s1">min_nodes</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-s1">max_nodes</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">3</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">aml_compute</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">AmlCompute</span>.<span class="pl-en">create</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ws</span>, <span class="pl-s1">name</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">aml_name</span>, <span class="pl-s1">provisioning_configuration</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">aml_config</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">aml_compute</span>.<span class="pl-en">wait_for_completion</span>(<span class="pl-s1">show_output</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">True</span>)

<span class="pl-s1">cts</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">ws</span>.<span class="pl-s1">compute_targets</span>
<span class="pl-s1">compute_target</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">cts</span>[<span class="pl-s1">aml_name</span>]</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">You can get the dataset from the workspace using the dataset name in the following way:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="dataset = ws.datasets['heart-failure-records']
df = dataset.to_pandas_dataframe()
df.describe()"><pre><span class="pl-s1">dataset</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">ws</span>.<span class="pl-s1">datasets</span>[<span class="pl-s">'heart-failure-records'</span>]
<span class="pl-s1">df</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">dataset</span>.<span class="pl-en">to_pandas_dataframe</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">df</span>.<span class="pl-en">describe</span>()</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-automl-configuration-and-training" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#automl-configuration-and-training"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>AutoML configuration and training</h4>
<p dir="auto">To set the AutoML configuration, use the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-train-automl-client/azureml.train.automl.automlconfig(class)?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">AutoMLConfig class</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">As described in the doc, there are a lot of parameters with which you can play with. For this project, we will use the following parameters:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>experiment_timeout_minutes</code>: The maximum amount of time (in minutes) that the experiment is allowed to run before it is automatically stopped and results are automatically made available</li>
<li><code>max_concurrent_iterations</code>: The maximum number of concurrent training iterations allowed for the experiment.</li>
<li><code>primary_metric</code>: The primary metric used to determine the experiment's status.</li>
<li><code>compute_target</code>: The Azure Machine Learning compute target to run the Automated Machine Learning experiment on.</li>
<li><code>task</code>: The type of task to run. Values can be 'classification', 'regression', or 'forecasting' depending on the type of automated ML problem to solve.</li>
<li><code>training_data</code>: The training data to be used within the experiment. It should contain both training features and a label column (optionally a sample weights column).</li>
<li><code>label_column_name</code>: The name of the label column.</li>
<li><code>path</code>: The full path to the Azure Machine Learning project folder.</li>
<li><code>enable_early_stopping</code>: Whether to enable early termination if the score is not improving in the short term.</li>
<li><code>featurization</code>: Indicator for whether the featurization step should be done automatically or not, or whether customized featurization should be used.</li>
<li><code>debug_log</code>: The log file to write debug information to.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from azureml.train.automl import AutoMLConfig

project_folder = './aml-project'

automl_settings = {
    &quot;experiment_timeout_minutes&quot;: 20,
    &quot;max_concurrent_iterations&quot;: 3,
    &quot;primary_metric&quot; : 'AUC_weighted'
}

automl_config = AutoMLConfig(compute_target=compute_target,
                             task = &quot;classification&quot;,
                             training_data=dataset,
                             label_column_name=&quot;DEATH_EVENT&quot;,
                             path = project_folder,  
                             enable_early_stopping= True,
                             featurization= 'auto',
                             debug_log = &quot;automl_errors.log&quot;,
                             **automl_settings
                            )"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">train</span>.<span class="pl-s1">automl</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">AutoMLConfig</span>

<span class="pl-s1">project_folder</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'./aml-project'</span>

<span class="pl-s1">automl_settings</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> {
    <span class="pl-s">"experiment_timeout_minutes"</span>: <span class="pl-c1">20</span>,
    <span class="pl-s">"max_concurrent_iterations"</span>: <span class="pl-c1">3</span>,
    <span class="pl-s">"primary_metric"</span> : <span class="pl-s">'AUC_weighted'</span>
}

<span class="pl-s1">automl_config</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">AutoMLConfig</span>(<span class="pl-s1">compute_target</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">compute_target</span>,
                             <span class="pl-s1">task</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"classification"</span>,
                             <span class="pl-s1">training_data</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">dataset</span>,
                             <span class="pl-s1">label_column_name</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s">"DEATH_EVENT"</span>,
                             <span class="pl-s1">path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">project_folder</span>,  
                             <span class="pl-s1">enable_early_stopping</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">True</span>,
                             <span class="pl-s1">featurization</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'auto'</span>,
                             <span class="pl-s1">debug_log</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"automl_errors.log"</span>,
                             <span class="pl-c1">**</span><span class="pl-s1">automl_settings</span>
                            )</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Now that you have your configuration set, you can train the model using the following code. This step can take up to an hour depending on your cluster size.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="remote_run = experiment.submit(automl_config)"><pre><span class="pl-s1">remote_run</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">experiment</span>.<span class="pl-en">submit</span>(<span class="pl-s1">automl_config</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">You can run the RunDetails widget to show the different experiments.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from azureml.widgets import RunDetails
RunDetails(remote_run).show()"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">widgets</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">RunDetails</span>
<span class="pl-v">RunDetails</span>(<span class="pl-s1">remote_run</span>).<span class="pl-en">show</span>()</pre></div>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-model-deployment-and-endpoint-consumption-with-the-azure-ml-sdk" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#model-deployment-and-endpoint-consumption-with-the-azure-ml-sdk"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Model deployment and endpoint consumption with the Azure ML SDK</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-saving-the-best-model" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#saving-the-best-model"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Saving the best model</h3>
<p dir="auto">The <code>remote_run</code> is an object of type <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-train-automl-client/azureml.train.automl.run.automlrun?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">AutoMLRun</a>. This object contains the method <code>get_output()</code> which returns the best run and the corresponding fitted model.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="best_run, fitted_model = remote_run.get_output()"><pre><span class="pl-s1">best_run</span>, <span class="pl-s1">fitted_model</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">remote_run</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_output</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">You can see the parameters used for the best model by just printing the fitted_model and see the properties of the best model by using the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-core/azureml.core.run(class)?view=azure-ml-py#azureml_core_Run_get_properties?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">get_properties()</a> method.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="best_run.get_properties()"><pre><span class="pl-s1">best_run</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_properties</span>()</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Now register the model with the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-train-automl-client/azureml.train.automl.run.automlrun?view=azure-ml-py#register-model-model-name-none--description-none--tags-none--iteration-none--metric-none-?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">register_model</a> method.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="model_name = best_run.properties['model_name']
script_file_name = 'inference/score.py'
best_run.download_file('outputs/scoring_file_v_1_0_0.py', 'inference/score.py')
description = &quot;aml heart failure project sdk&quot;
model = best_run.register_model(
    model_name = model_name,
    model_path = './outputs/',
    description = description,
    tags = None
)"><pre><span class="pl-s1">model_name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">best_run</span>.<span class="pl-s1">properties</span>[<span class="pl-s">'model_name'</span>]
<span class="pl-s1">script_file_name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'inference/score.py'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">best_run</span>.<span class="pl-en">download_file</span>(<span class="pl-s">'outputs/scoring_file_v_1_0_0.py'</span>, <span class="pl-s">'inference/score.py'</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">description</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">"aml heart failure project sdk"</span>
<span class="pl-s1">model</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">best_run</span>.<span class="pl-en">register_model</span>(
    <span class="pl-s1">model_name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">model_name</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">model_path</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'./outputs/'</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">description</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">description</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">tags</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>
)</pre></div>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-model-deployment" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#model-deployment"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Model deployment</h3>
<p dir="auto">Once the best model is saved, we can deploy it with the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-core/azureml.core.model.inferenceconfig?view=azure-ml-py?ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">InferenceConfig</a> class. InferenceConfig represents the configuration settings for a custom environment used for deployment. The <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-core/azureml.core.webservice.aciwebservice?view=azure-ml-py" rel="nofollow">AciWebservice</a> class represents a Machine Learning model deployed as a web service endpoint on Azure Container Instances. A deployed service is created from a model, script, and associated files. The resulting web service is a load-balanced, HTTP endpoint with a REST API. You can send data to this API and receive the prediction returned by the model.</p>
<p dir="auto">The model is deployed using the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/azureml-core/azureml.core.model(class)?view=azure-ml-py#deploy-workspace--name--models--inference-config-none--deployment-config-none--deployment-target-none--overwrite-false--show-output-false-?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">deploy</a> method.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="from azureml.core.model import InferenceConfig, Model
from azureml.core.webservice import AciWebservice

inference_config = InferenceConfig(entry_script=script_file_name, environment=best_run.get_environment())

aciconfig = AciWebservice.deploy_configuration(
    cpu_cores = 1,
    memory_gb = 1,
    tags = {'type': &quot;automl-heart-failure-prediction&quot;},
    description = 'Sample service for AutoML Heart Failure Prediction'
)

aci_service_name = 'automl-hf-sdk'
aci_service = Model.deploy(ws, aci_service_name, [model], inference_config, aciconfig)
aci_service.wait_for_deployment(True)
print(aci_service.state)"><pre><span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">core</span>.<span class="pl-s1">model</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">InferenceConfig</span>, <span class="pl-v">Model</span>
<span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s1">azureml</span>.<span class="pl-s1">core</span>.<span class="pl-s1">webservice</span> <span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-v">AciWebservice</span>

<span class="pl-s1">inference_config</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">InferenceConfig</span>(<span class="pl-s1">entry_script</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">script_file_name</span>, <span class="pl-s1">environment</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">best_run</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_environment</span>())

<span class="pl-s1">aciconfig</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">AciWebservice</span>.<span class="pl-en">deploy_configuration</span>(
    <span class="pl-s1">cpu_cores</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">memory_gb</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>,
    <span class="pl-s1">tags</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> {<span class="pl-s">'type'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"automl-heart-failure-prediction"</span>},
    <span class="pl-s1">description</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'Sample service for AutoML Heart Failure Prediction'</span>
)

<span class="pl-s1">aci_service_name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'automl-hf-sdk'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">aci_service</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Model</span>.<span class="pl-en">deploy</span>(<span class="pl-s1">ws</span>, <span class="pl-s1">aci_service_name</span>, [<span class="pl-s1">model</span>], <span class="pl-s1">inference_config</span>, <span class="pl-s1">aciconfig</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">aci_service</span>.<span class="pl-en">wait_for_deployment</span>(<span class="pl-c1">True</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">aci_service</span>.<span class="pl-s1">state</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This step should take a few minutes.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-endpoint-consumption" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#endpoint-consumption"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Endpoint consumption</h3>
<p dir="auto">You consume your endpoint by creating a sample input:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="data = {
    &quot;data&quot;:
    [
        {
            'age': &quot;60&quot;,
            'anaemia': &quot;false&quot;,
            'creatinine_phosphokinase': &quot;500&quot;,
            'diabetes': &quot;false&quot;,
            'ejection_fraction': &quot;38&quot;,
            'high_blood_pressure': &quot;false&quot;,
            'platelets': &quot;260000&quot;,
            'serum_creatinine': &quot;1.40&quot;,
            'serum_sodium': &quot;137&quot;,
            'sex': &quot;false&quot;,
            'smoking': &quot;false&quot;,
            'time': &quot;130&quot;,
        },
    ],
}

test_sample = str.encode(json.dumps(data))"><pre><span class="pl-s1">data</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> {
    <span class="pl-s">"data"</span>:
    [
        {
            <span class="pl-s">'age'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"60"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'anaemia'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"false"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'creatinine_phosphokinase'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"500"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'diabetes'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"false"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'ejection_fraction'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"38"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'high_blood_pressure'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"false"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'platelets'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"260000"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'serum_creatinine'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"1.40"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'serum_sodium'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"137"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'sex'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"false"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'smoking'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"false"</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">'time'</span>: <span class="pl-s">"130"</span>,
        },
    ],
}

<span class="pl-s1">test_sample</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">str</span>.<span class="pl-en">encode</span>(<span class="pl-s1">json</span>.<span class="pl-en">dumps</span>(<span class="pl-s1">data</span>))</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And then you can send this input to your model for prediction :</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="response = aci_service.run(input_data=test_sample)
response"><pre><span class="pl-s1">response</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">aci_service</span>.<span class="pl-en">run</span>(<span class="pl-s1">input_data</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">test_sample</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">response</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This should output <code>'{"result": [false]}'</code>. This means that the patient input we sent to the endpoint generated the prediction <code>false</code> which means this person is not likely to have a heart attack.</p>
<p dir="auto">Congratulations! You just consumed the model deployed and trained on Azure ML with the Azure ML SDK!</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Once you are done with the project, don't forget to delete all the resources."><pre lang="{note}" class="notranslate"><code>Once you are done with the project, don't forget to delete all the resources.
</code></pre></div>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-your-turn-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#your-turn-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Your turn! <g-emoji class="g-emoji" alias="rocket" fallback-src="https://github.githubassets.com/images/icons/emoji/unicode/1f680.png"></g-emoji></h2>
<p dir="auto">There are many other things you can do through the SDK, unfortunately, we can not view them all in this section. But good news, learning how to skim through the SDK documentation can take you a long way on your own. Have a look at the Azure ML SDK documentation and find the <code>Pipeline</code> class that allows you to create pipelines. A Pipeline is a collection of steps which can be executed as a workflow.</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="**HINT:** Go to the [SDK documentation](https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/overview/azure/ml/?view=azure-ml-py?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109) and type keywords in the search bar like &quot;Pipeline&quot;. You should have the `azureml.pipeline.core.Pipeline` class in the search results."><pre lang="{note}" class="notranslate"><code>**HINT:** Go to the [SDK documentation](https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/overview/azure/ml/?view=azure-ml-py?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109) and type keywords in the search bar like "Pipeline". You should have the `azureml.pipeline.core.Pipeline` class in the search results.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Assignment - <a href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/open-machine-learning-jupyter-book/assignments/data-science/data-science-project-using-azure-ml-sdk.md">Data Science project using Azure ML SDK</a></p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-self-study" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#self-study"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Self study</h2>
<p dir="auto">In this section, you learned how to train, deploy and consume a model to predict heart failure risk with the Azure ML SDK in the cloud. Check this <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/python/api/overview/azure/ml/?view=azure-ml-py?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">documentation</a> for further information about the Azure ML SDK. Try to create your own model with the Azure ML SDK.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-acknowledgments" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#acknowledgments"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Acknowledgments</h2>

<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-the-low-codeno-code-way" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#the-low-codeno-code-way"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>The "low code/no code" way</h1>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-what-is-azure-machine-learningml" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#what-is-azure-machine-learningml"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>What is Azure Machine Learning(ML)?</h2>
<p dir="auto">The Azure cloud platform is more than 200 products and cloud services designed to help you bring new solutions to life. Data scientists expend a lot of effort exploring and pre-processing data and trying various types of model-training algorithms to produce accurate models. These tasks are time-consuming and often make inefficient use of expensive compute hardware.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/machine-learning/overview-what-is-azure-machine-learning?WT.mc_id=academic-77958-bethanycheum&amp;ocid=AID3041109" rel="nofollow">Azure ML</a> is a cloud-based platform for building and operating Machine Learning solutions in Azure. It includes a wide range of features and capabilities that help data scientists prepare data, train models, publish predictive services, and monitor their usage. Most importantly, it helps them to increase their efficiency by automating many of the time-consuming tasks associated with training models; and it enables them to use cloud-based compute resources that scale effectively, to handle large volumes of data while incurring costs only when actually used.</p>
<p dir="auto">Azure ML provides all the tools developers and data scientists need for their Machine Learning workflows. These include:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Azure Machine Learning Studio</strong>: it is a web portal in Azure Machine Learning for low-code and no-code options for model training, deployment, automation, tracking and asset management. The studio integrates with the Azure Machine Learning SDK for a seamless experience.</li>
<li><strong>Jupyter Notebooks</strong>: quickly prototype and test ML models.</li>
<li><strong>Azure Machine Learning Designer</strong>: allows to drag-n-drop modules to build experiments and then deploy pipelines in a low-code environment.</li>
<li><strong>Automated Machine Learning UI (AutoML)</strong> : automates iterative tasks of Machine Learning model development, allowing to build Machine Learning models with high scale, efficiency, and productivity, all while sustaining model quality.</li>
<li><strong>Data Labelling</strong>: an assisted ML tool to automatically label data.</li>
<li><strong>Machine Learning extension for Visual Studio Code</strong>: provides a full-featured development environment for building and managing Machine Learning projects.</li>
<li><strong>Machine Learning CLI</strong>: provides commands for managing Azure ML resources from the command line.</li>
<li><strong>Integration with open-source frameworks</strong> such as PyTorch, TensorFlow, Scikit-learn and many more for training, deploying and managing the end-to-end Machine Learning process.</li>
<li><strong>MLflow</strong>: It is an open-source library for managing the life cycle of your Lachine Learning experiments. <strong>MLflow Tracking</strong> is a component of MLflow that logs and tracks your training run metrics and model artifacts, irrespective of your experiment's environment.</li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-the-heart-failure-prediction-project" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#the-heart-failure-prediction-project"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>The heart failure prediction project</h2>
<p dir="auto">There is no doubt that making and building projects are the best way to put your skills and knowledge to the test. In this section, we are going to explore two different ways of building a data science project for the prediction of heart failure attacks in Azure ML Studio, through Low code/No code and through the Azure ML SDK as shown in the following schema:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/open-academy/machine-learning/blob/main/images/project-schema.png"><img src="/open-academy/machine-learning/raw/main/images/project-schema.png" alt="project-schema" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Each way has its own pros and cons. The Low code/No code way is easier to start with as it involves interacting with a GUI (Graphical User Interface), with no prior knowledge of code required. This method enables quick testing of the project's viability and to create POC (Proof Of Concept). However, as the project grows and things need to be production ready, it is not feasible to create resources through GUI. We need to programmatically automate everything, from the creation of resources to the deployment of a model. This is where knowing how to use the Azure ML SDK becomes crucial.</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>

</tr>
</thead>

<td>Not required</td>

</tr>

<td>Fast and easy</td>

<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-the-heart-failure-dataset" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#the-heart-failure-dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>The heart failure dataset</h2>
<p dir="auto">Cardiovascular diseases (CVDs) are the number 1 cause of death globally, accounting for 31% of all deaths worldwide. Environmental and behavioral risk factors such as use of tobacco, unhealthy diet and obesity, physical inactivity and harmful use of alcohol could be used as features for estimation models. Being able to estimate the probability of the development of a CVD could be of great use to prevent attacks in high-risk people.</p>
<p dir="auto">Kaggle has made a <a href="https://www.kaggle.com/andrewmvd/heart-failure-clinical-data" rel="nofollow">Heart Failure dataset</a> publicly available, that we are going to use for this project. You can download the dataset now. This is a tabular dataset with 13 columns (12 features and 1 target variable) and 299 rows.</p>
